<p><b>BitTorrent</b> is a communications <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protocol_(computing)" title="Protocol (computing)">protocol</a> of <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer_file_sharing" title="Peer-to-peer file sharing">peer-to-peer file sharing</a> ("P2P") which is used to distribute <a href="/wiki/Data_(computing)" title="Data (computing)">data</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_file" title="Electronic file">electronic files</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>. BitTorrent is one of the most common protocols for transferring large files, such as <a href="/wiki/Digital_video" title="Digital video">digital video</a> files containing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TV_show" title="TV show">TV shows</a> or <a href="/wiki/Video_clip" title="Video clip">video clips</a> or <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio" title="Digital audio">digital audio</a> files containing <a href="/wiki/Song" title="Song">songs</a>. Peer-to-peer networks have been estimated to collectively account for approximately 43% to 70% of all <a href="/wiki/Internet_traffic" title="Internet traffic">Internet traffic</a> (depending on location) as of February 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BitTorrent&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> In November 2004, BitTorrent was responsible for 25% of all Internet traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> As of February 2013, BitTorrent was responsible for 3.35% of all worldwide <a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)" title="Bandwidth (computing)">bandwidth</a>, more than half of the 6% of total bandwidth dedicated to file sharing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>To send or receive files, a person uses a <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_BitTorrent_clients" title="Comparison of BitTorrent clients">BitTorrent client</a> on his or her <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>-connected <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computer</a>. A BitTorrent client is a computer program that implements the BitTorrent protocol. Popular clients include <a href="/wiki/%CE%9CTorrent" title="ΜTorrent">μTorrent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xunlei" title="Xunlei">Xunlei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(BitTorrent_client)" title="Transmission (BitTorrent client)">Transmission</a>, <a href="/wiki/QBittorrent" title="QBittorrent">qBittorrent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vuze" title="Vuze">Vuze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deluge_(software)" title="Deluge (software)">Deluge</a>, <a href="/wiki/BitComet" title="BitComet">BitComet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tixati" title="Tixati">Tixati</a>. <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent_tracker" title="BitTorrent tracker">BitTorrent trackers</a> provide a list of files available for transfer, and allow the client to find peer users known as <i>seeds</i> who may transfer the files.</p>
<p>Programmer <a href="/wiki/Bram_Cohen" title="Bram Cohen">Bram Cohen</a>, a former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York" title="University at Buffalo, The State University of New York">University at Buffalo</a> student,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> designed the protocol in April 2001 and released the first available version on 2 July 2001,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BC_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-BC-5">[5]</a></sup> and the most recent version in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Protocol1.0_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Protocol1.0-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_BitTorrent_clients" title="Comparison of BitTorrent clients">BitTorrent clients</a> are available for a variety of <a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">computing platforms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_BitTorrent_clients#Operating_system_support" title="Comparison of BitTorrent clients">operating systems</a> including an official client released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BitTorrent,_Inc." title="BitTorrent, Inc.">BitTorrent, Inc.</a></p>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BitTorrent&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, BitTorrent has 15–27 million concurrent users at any time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> As of January 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BitTorrent&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, BitTorrent is utilized by 150 million active users. Based on this figure, the total number of monthly BitTorrent users may be estimated to more than a quarter of a billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:359px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torrentcomp_small.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="357" height="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3d/Torrentcomp_small.gif" width="357"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torrentcomp_small.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Animation of <a href="/wiki/Communications_protocol" title="Communications protocol">protocol</a> use: The colored dots beneath each computer in the animation represent different parts of the <a href="/wiki/File_sharing" title="File sharing">file being shared</a>. By the time a copy to a destination computer of each of those parts completes, a copy to another destination computer of that part (or other parts) is already taking place between users. The <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent_tracker" title="BitTorrent tracker">tracker</a> (<a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">server</a>) provides only a single copy of the file, and all the users clone its parts from one another.</div>
</div>
</div>
